## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: nonlinear oscillator dynamics
**Analysis**: This task models the acceleration (dv/dt) of a nonlinear harmonic oscillator as a function of position x, velocity v, and time t. The acceleration encodes the forces acting on the system, which may include nonlinear restoring forces, damping, and external driving.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Simple harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (linear restoring force)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring + linear damping)
- Driven damped oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (with periodic driving)
- Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Damped Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (Duffing + damping)
- Driven damped Duffing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (full Duffing equation)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (1 - c2 * x**2) * v (nonlinear damping)
- Quintic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order restoring force)
- Quadratic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 (asymmetric restoring force)
- Softening/hardening spring: dv_dt = c0 * x * (1 + c1 * x**2) (amplitude-dependent stiffness)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * (1 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x (time-varying stiffness)
- Nonlinear damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * x**2 (position-dependent damping)
- Cubic damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (velocity-dependent nonlinear damping)
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (Rayleigh-type nonlinear damping)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x**3, x**5) preserve symmetry of oscillation about equilibrium — expect odd polynomial terms in x for symmetric potentials
- Even-power terms in x (x**2, x**4) indicate broken symmetry / asymmetric potential wells
- Velocity-dependent terms proportional to v indicate energy dissipation or injection (damping/driving)
- Products of x**2 and v (e.g., x**2 * v) indicate amplitude-dependent or nonlinear damping characteristic of Van der Pol-type systems
- Sinusoidal functions of time sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) indicate external periodic forcing
- Time appearing only inside trigonometric functions suggests autonomous dynamics with periodic driving, not explicit time dependence of parameters
- Cubic terms in x with opposite sign to linear term (c0*x + c1*x**3 where c0 and c1 have same sign for restoring) indicate Duffing-type hardening or softening springs
- Absence of explicit time dependence suggests an autonomous system where energy considerations (conservative or dissipative) fully govern dynamics

GT: F0*sin(t) - alpha*v**c0 - beta*exp(-Abs(v))*v - omega0**c1*x**c2
Candidate formulas: 50

I need to determine if any candidate formula can match the GT:

**GT:** `-0.0907*v**3 - 0.5945*v*exp(-|v|) - 2.9429*x**3 + 0.5691*sin(t)`

The GT has four terms:
1. `c*x**3` (cubic in x)
2. `c*sin(t)` (sine of t with frequency 1)
3. `c*v**3` (cubic in v)
4. `c*v*exp(-|v|)` (v times exponential of -|v|)

The key challenge is the term `v*exp(-|v|)`. This involves an absolute value, making it non-analytic. Let me check each candidate for the ability to reproduce all four terms.

**Candidates with v**c (power of v) terms:** Candidates 1-5, 8, 11, 15, 16 have `v**c` terms plus linear `v` terms. But `v**3 + c*v` cannot equal `v**3 + c*v*exp(-|v|)` for all v.

**Candidates with log terms (6, 10, 25, 41, 43):** `log(c*v+1)` cannot reproduce `v*exp(-|v|)`.

**Candidates with exp(c*v) terms (12-21):** These have `exp(c5*v)` which is exponential in v, not `exp(-|v|)`. Since `exp(c*v)` doesn't handle the absolute value, it can't match `exp(-|v|)` for both positive and negative v simultaneously. However, let me think more carefully...

For `v*exp(-|v|)`: when v>0, this is `v*exp(-v)`; when v<0, this is `v*exp(v)`. No single `exp(c*v)` can capture both branches.

**Candidates with rational terms in v (9, 13, 14, 17-21, 24):** Rational functions of v can't match `v*exp(-|v|)`.

**Candidates with v*x terms (26, 28, 33, 34, 35, 39, 40):** These mix v and x, but GT has no such cross-terms. Setting those coefficients to 0 leaves only linear v terms, which can't match `v*exp(-|v|)`.

**Candidates with v*(x+c)**4 type terms (29-32, 34):** Same issue - cross terms or pure v terms only.

**Candidates with t-dependent v terms (36, 37, 43, 45):** These have v multiplied by functions of t, which doesn't appear in GT.

**Candidates with cos(c*t) terms (25, 33, 37, 38, 46-50):** `c1*sin(c2*t+c3) + c5*cos(c6*t)` - if c3=0 and c6=1, this gives `c1*sin(t) + c5*cos(t)`. This can't simplify to just `sin(t)` unless c5=0 (setting cos term to 0). But then we're left with the same problem of matching `v*exp(-|v|)` with the remaining v terms.

**Candidate 48:** `c0*x + c1*x**3 + c2*sin(c3*t+c4) + c5*v + c6*cos(c7*t)` - set c0=0, c6=0, leaves `c1*x**3 + c2*sin(c3*t+c4) + c5*v`. Linear v can't match `v**3 + v*exp(-|v|)`.

None of the candidates contain both a `v**3` term AND a `v*exp(-|v|)` term (or anything that could reproduce `v*exp(-|v|)`). The absolute value in `exp(-|v|)` is particularly problematic - no candidate has absolute value functions.

The closest candidates are those with `v**c + c*v` (like 3, 4, 15), which could give `v**3 + c*v`, but `c*v ≠ c*v*exp(-|v|)`.

Candidates with `exp(c*v)` terms plus `v/(cv+c)` rational terms might approximate but cannot exactly equal `v*exp(-|v|)` due to the absolute value.

After careful analysis, **no candidate** can exactly reproduce the GT expression `-0.0907*v**3 - 0.5945*v*exp(-|v|) - 2.9429*x**3 + 0.5691*sin(t)` for all values of x, t, v.
